**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is April, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

    First Check After Step 5

    First Check After Step 6

    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

• Each article was examined for its headline content and then uniquely assigned to one of our seven areas.
• For Immigration topics, a clear distinction was maintained between the specific Abrego Garcia case (Topic 1.1), general deportation policies (Topic 1.2), border operations (Topic 1.3), and proposals for international detention (Topic 1.4).
• Articles on trade and tariffs were split between those addressing tariff policy directly (Topic 2.1), US–China relations (Topic 2.2), international responses (Topic 2.3), and domestic economic impacts (Topic 2.4).
• Executive actions and legal challenges were mapped under Area 3 with subtopics for executive orders (3.1), judicial rulings (3.2), constitutional disputes (3.3), and federal–state conflicts (3.4).
• Government Efficiency issues (especially those involving DOGE, agency shake-ups, media policy, or funding) were grouped under Area 4.
• Domestic policy matters (health, environment, social safety net, education) were placed in Area 5.
• Finally, political dynamics—including public protests, internal party strategy, and public figures’ statements—were included in Area 6, while international diplomacy (embassy changes, military deployments, allied relations) was assigned to Area 7.

# Daily Briefing: April 2025

## 1. International Relations and Diplomacy

### 1.1 Ukraine Policy and Allied Relations  
President Trump has shifted U.S. positioning on the Ukraine conflict by publicly blaming President Zelensky for starting the war with Russia, making these comments just one day after a significant Russian attack [1]. Relations with traditional allies show signs of strain, with Greenland reportedly developing closer ties with China in what's characterized as a deliberate rebuff to the Trump administration [2]. Denmark has published a pointed message questioning American skepticism toward its allegiance [3], while administration officials are reportedly "fed up" with European efforts to strengthen Ukraine [4].

### 1.2 Military and Diplomatic Presence  
Two U.S. troops have been killed in a vehicle rollover accident during a mission at the southern border [1]. On the diplomatic front, the administration is pursuing a significant reduction in U.S. global presence, with plans to close approximately 30 overseas embassies and consulates [2].

## 2. Immigration and Border Enforcement

### 2.1 Abrego Garcia Deportation Case  
The case of Kilmar Abrego Garcia, deported to El Salvador, has escalated into what some Democratic lawmakers are calling a "constitutional crisis" [1]. Despite Supreme Court rulings, the administration has reportedly refused to comply with court orders to secure his return [2], with one judge explicitly reminding officials "you lost" at the Supreme Court [3]. A federal judge has ordered the Justice Department to provide detailed information about efforts to return Garcia [4]. Allegations linking him to MS-13 have been questioned, reportedly stemming from "double hearsay" in a document written by a police detective who was later suspended [5]. The Justice Department has fired an immigration lawyer who worked on the case [6], while Democratic lawmakers are planning trips to El Salvador to check on Garcia's welfare [7].

Beyond the Garcia case, broader immigration policies continue to evolve. International student visas are being revoked under new guidelines [1], a U.S. judge has ruled that the Justice Department can cut funding for legal guidance for people facing deportation [2], and reports indicate Trump officials are using federal agencies to deliberately create difficult conditions for undocumented immigrants [3]. In a significant policy development, the White House has confirmed it is exploring the legality of sending U.S. citizens to foreign prisons [4], prompting protests with critics warning that "homegrowns are next" [5].

### 4.1 Executive Actions and Judicial Responses

## 5. Government Reorganization and DOGE Activities

### 5.1 Media and Agency Changes  
The White House has introduced a policy limiting wire services' access to the president [1] and has characterized NPR and PBS as a "grift," announcing plans to ask Congress to rescind their funding [2]. In personnel changes, the Pentagon has removed senior adviser Dan Caldwell during an investigation into information leaks [3]. The Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), led by Elon Musk, has claimed success in identifying $382 million in unemployment fraud, though reports indicate this fraud had already been discovered by the government years earlier [4]. A top House Democrat has raised concerns about DOGE's data access at the National Labor Relations Board (NLRB), characterizing it as potential "technological malfeasance" [5].

## 7. Political Dynamics and Public Response

### 7.1 Democratic Party Strategy  
Internal Democratic Party dynamics show signs of strategic division. David Hogg, a Parkland shooting survivor who now serves as DNC Vice Chair, has announced plans to support primary challenges against Democratic incumbents [1] in what Politico describes as an "unprecedented move" [2]. Polling indicates that 72% of Democrats want the party to abandon its centrist approach to countering Trump [3]. Former President Biden has made his first public remarks since leaving office, stating that America "can't go on like this as a divided nation" [4].
